Introduction and Adoption of Subscription -Based Memberships 
• Higher share of operator revenues from recurring subscriptions vs. past 
recessions, providing a ballast in potential future downturns 
110 Car wash subscription -based plans had not experienced widespread 
adoption by the time of the Great Recession 
Given the recurring nature of subscriptions, these revenues have 
proven to be more resilient through an economic downturn

Emergence of the Express Format Model 
• Superior model - ability to generate strong EBITDA and cash flow in a 
downturn due to low fixed costs and limited labor requirements 
• Viewed as an efficient and affordable essential car maintenance solution 
(average single-wash ticket < $10.00), positioned to capture consumer share 
from more expensive car wash formats 
Professionalization and Consolidation 
• Operators and investors increasingly professionalizing operations, 
driving a shift to highly efficient and advanced operating models 
• Increasing scale and market diversity significantly reducing the impact 
of a potential economic downturn 
105 - Supplemented by increasing environmental regulations restricting - home wash, leading car owners to turn to professional services 
Well -positioned to mitigate downside performance 
2018 2019 2020 from a potential future recession

NSECTOR -WIDE TRANSITION TO SUBSCRIPTION -BASED SERVICES ac irn iii 
Emerging shift from single-wash customers to recurring, subscription-based offerings "locks in" 
consumers' share of wallet and drives lifetime value while relying less on impulse purchases 
Industry -Wide Evolution of Consumer Behavior... ...Leading to the Rise of the Subscription Economy 
Evolving consumer behavior is (fraying a shift in the 
retail proposition and disrupting traditional operating models 
Increased Demand for Convenience 
Consumers want the retail and service experience to be fast, simple 
and efficient 
Customers are more likely to visit a physical service location 
because they are looking for something specific 
Desire for Frictionless Shopping &Services 
Consumers like their shopping journey between each channel and 
touchpoint to be a seamless, connected experience 
Driven by Gen Z and millennials, retailers are embracing mobile 
channels to help customers learn about and access their offerings 
Expectation Of Personalization 
With significant amounts of data, companies can continuously 
optimize / personalize the customer experience 
Consumers are increasingly willing to provide necessary 
personal data to allow for personalized experiences 
Retailtainment 
Shopping is viewed as an experience rather than a chore, driving a 
convergence of leisure, entertainment and merchandising 
widers that create a more i rnmersive experience tend to have 
ter customer stickiness

WASH Discussion and Analysis 
• Splash requires low net working capital to fund its daily 
operations 
• The Company collects credit card payments from customers at 
the point of Sal and monthly subscription payments are 
charged to constiiffers each month, limiting any accounts 
receivable 
"v 
• Inventoryeprimarily comprised of chemicals, supplies and 
misdeLlatveous items stored in warehouses to ensure consistent 
uptitne and availability of supplies 
Discussion and Analysis 
• Growth Capital Expenditures 
- De Novo Site Development -Forecasted to be $5.0 to $7.5 million 
per site; development is generally fully funded with SLB 
proceeds 
- Existing Site hnprovenwnts - Facelifts and equipment upgrades at 
acquired sites to ensure all sites are operating to Splash's 
standards 
• Maintenance Capital Expenditures - Annual recurring costs to 
maintain facilities and equipment at sites; conservative forecast 
of $24 thousand (-1% of revenues) per site per year 
• Low working capital requirement and maintenance capital 
expenditures result in 90%+ free cash flow conversion 
• Acquisition Purchase Consideration  -$37.5 million spent 
to -date in 2022 and 10 additional acquisitions expected to be 
completed by the end of the year

Discussion and Analysis 
• Past Acauisition Transaction Expenses - Elimination of non-operational 
transaction expenses and broker fees paid on past acquisitions 
• Construction Costs - Adjustment to capitalize construction costs of de novo 
units that were expensed 
• Single-Wash Price Increase - Normalizes the impact of single wash and 
membership price increases that went into effect in March 2022 as if they had 
been effective for the entire 12-month period 
• Non-Recurring Professional Service Expenses - Addback of non-recurring 
professional fees, including advisory fees and other consulting expenses 
• PPP loan forgiveness - Removal of non-recurring income related to the 
forgiveness of i'l'l' loan 
• Rent Expense Normalization - Pro forma rent expense as if sale and leasebacks 
had been executed on all currently leased sites during all periods 
• Other Diligence Adjustments - Includes miscellaneous adjustments including 
normalization of out-of-period bonuses, one-time commission costs, lease 
adjustments under ASU842 and loss on sale of assets 
• Existing Sites Maturing - Reflects the mature-site performance of 9 existing 
operating locations using a conservative 2-year maturation period 
• Existing Site Upgrade - Reflects pro forma EBITDA of 12 existing sites that are 
currently undergoing significant operational upgrades as if they were 
operating as mature sites (2 years following completion of renovations) 
• In-Development Sites - Reflects the mature performance of 23 development 
sites that are currently in various stages of construction or permitting and 
expected to open before the end of 2023, using a conservative 2-year 
maturation period 
• identified Acquisitions adiustment - Reflects the pro forma contribution of 
10 sites that are expected to be acquired during the second half of 2022, 
including 8 sites that are currently under LOI and pending completion

Site-Level Operating Expenses 
Fixed and semi-variable costs associated with wash 
operations are expected to decline modestly as a percentage 
of revenues at each individual location as each unit scales; 
operating costs in aggregate increase slightly as a percentage 
of revepuiftwough 2027 due to the shift towards express 
wash format, where proportionately more of the unit's 
expenses are in operating expenses (vs. cost of goods sold) 
but with higher site-level EBITDAR margins 
• Advertising - Total expenditure made regionally but 
allocated to individual sites; mature sites increase 
expenditure by 2.0% annually 
• Utilities  - Semi-variable utilities expenses including water, 
electric and internee forecasted as 85.0% fixed with 
• Utilities M Repairs and Supplies Fees modest annual increases, and 15.0% variable based on a

e ala CAR WASH 
Discussion and Analysis 
Variable and Hybrid Site-Level  Cost of Goods Sold 
Includes the direct variable costs associated with cleaning of 
customer vehicles and the operation of waiting room stores; 
gross margins are expected to increase primarily as a result of 
the continued shift in revenue mix towards subscription 
membership programs and the shift in revenues towards the 
express wash format, which has lower site -level labor costs 
and higher gross margins than other comparable wash 
formats 
• Cleaning Fluids-  Includes the direct costs of detergents 
and other chemicals measured as a cost per car; Splash's 
chemicals costs average $0.74 per car in 2022E and are 
forecasted to decrease by $0.02 per car annually as the 
Company realizes favorable leverage on its chemical costs 
purchases from greater scale 
• Site-Level Labor - Includes the hourly wage costs and 
volume -based sales commissions paid to site -level 
employees; site -level labor costs are forecasted to increase 
by 3.0% annually to reflect customary wage increases and 
growth in commission -generating sales volumes 
• Store Costs - Operating costs associated with the operation 
of attached gift stores in the customer waiting areas of 
certain Splash locations; costs are forecasted to increase by 
2.0% annually 
• Other Costs of Goods Sold - Miscellaneous other costs 
associated with non -car wash services representing less 
than 1.0% of total COGS; forecasted to increase by 
2.0% annually

flBASIS OF FINANCIAL PRESENTATION e aM  L4/ CAN WaSil 
Historical and Estimated Financials 
• Splash's historical financial results presented herein are derived from internal and audited financial statements and have been adjusted for certain one-time, 
non-recurring items; details of these adjustments are presented on slide 57 
• A Quality of Earnings review has been prepared by a third -party accounting firm for the years ended December 31, 2019, December 31, 2020, December 31, 2021 
and the trailing twelve-month period ended March 31, 2022, the details of which will be made available at a later date 
• Estimated financial statements for 2022E include Quality of Earnings financials through March, internal adjusted financials for April and management's forecast for 
May through December 
• 2020 financials presented throughout the presentation exclude any normalization adjustment for the impact of COVID-19 
• Historical and estimated financials exclude acquisitions for which the Company is in the process of negotiating a LO! 
• Pro forma revenues and EBITDA for LTM March 2022 and 2022E l'F are presented using a conservative two-year maturation analysis as if: 
- 9 locations opened in the last two years (as of LTM March 2022) are performing at a mature level, based on detailed site-level budgets and forecasts 
- 12 existing unit upgrade locations that are undergoing or expected to undergo capex upgrades are performing at a mature level 
- 23 development locations that are scheduled to open in the next fifteen months are performing at a mature level, based on the detailed site-level forecasts and 
budgets that are informed by actual performance of previous greenfield locations 
Protected Financials 12023P to 2027P1 
• The Company's financial projections have been prepared by management and represent their assessment of expected financial performance through 20271' 
• The financial projections have been prepared on an annual basis utilizing detailed assumptions regarding the following: 
- Revenue growth by individual site within each respective market, segmented by service offering 
- Same-store sales growth for existing mature sites informed by single-wash volume, average ticket, membership count and effective membership price 
- Cost per car, other direct costs of service, gross margin and operating expenses by individual site 
- Regional support, corporate overhead, maintenance capital expenditures and capital expenditures related to de novo sites on a consolidated basis, net of 
anticipated sale lease-back proceeds 
• Consistent with the Company's plans to continue its organic greenfield growth strategy, management's projections include the development of additional sites 
based on the following assumptions, supported by detailed, bottoms-up analyses: 
- Revenue and EBITDA maturation based on Splash's realized performance with recently completed greenfield developments 
- Capital investment consistent with recent experience from completed greenfield developments and further refined for site-specific factors 
• By their nature, projections reflect estimates arid assumptions that are subject to economic, regulatory, geopolitical and competitive uncertainties that are beyond 
management's and the Company's control 
Acquisition Assumptions (2022E to 2027P) 
• Conservatively assumes the acquisition of 10 sites in 2H 2022 (including 8 sites under L01), 10 sites in 2023, 15 sites in 2024, 20 sites in 2025,25 sites in 2026 and 
30 sites in 2027, for a total of 110 sites added to the platform over the next five years via acquisition 
- For comparison, the Company completed 23 site acquisitions in 2021 and has completed 8 site acquisitions YTD June 2022 
• Cumulative revenues of $120.4 million and EBITDA of $58.5 million added through acquisition by 2027

De Novo Selection and Grand Opening Playbook 
O Site Identification, Development and Construction 
• Data -driven real estate selection led by 14-member development team 
that has evaluated over 300 sites in the past three years, focused on site 
characteristics, demographics and competitive landscape 
• Location relative to existing Splash sites and wash format are critical in 
determining potential network benefits and/or cannibalization 
O Construction Completion: 6 to 8 Months Post Permitting Approval 
Sitework crews on staff with owned light equipment to accelerate 
construction and reduce cost 
Relationships with trusted local contractors 
O Sale and Leaseback Proceeds 7." • Relationships with two REIT partners that offer immediate funding for land 
and construction, with full sale and leaseback completed upon certificate of 
occupancy 
• Proceeds generally cover the full cost of development, supported by 3-year 
maturation credit provided by REIT partnci • 
O Grand Opening Marketing Playbook and Maturation

velocity during the first 3 months of opening

Splash's focus on recruiting, training and empowering talent ensures a consistent customer

Employee Overview Employee Count by Type (1) 
• Splash's unique employee -centric culture is an essential component and driver 
of competitive differentiation 
- Enhanced individual accountability and greater sense of ownership 
empower employees at all levels 
- Extensive career advancement and professional development 
opportunities within the platform 
- Launched the Culture Index initiative in 2020 as a tool to enhance

IILONG ISLAND REGIONAL OVERVIEW 
Market Strategy 
The Long Island region was established in 2022 through the 
acquisition of two operating sites and one in-development site 
• Splash management has been opportunistically targeting the 
Long Island market for several years 
• Acquired sites in Al- locations in high -traffic, high -income 
neighborhoods in Nassau and Suffolk counties 
Hyper -fragmented competition and attractive demand dynamics 
provide Splash with a unique opportunity to deploy its proven 
land -and -expand model 
• Opportunity to extract significant operational and marketing 
synergies due to proximity to the Metro -North network 
• Significant whitespace opportunity to further penetrate the 
market through acquisitions; 3 sites currently under LOI 
• Since entry, management has evaluated 5+ additional acquisiti 
sites and potential de novos, many of which were identified 
acquired site founders retained as development partners

I UPSTATE NEW YORK REGIONAL OVERVIEW 
Market Strategy 
• Splash's Upstate New York network has been developed over the 
last 40+ years through a combination of de novo developments 
and strategic acquisitions 
• Sites are concentrated around the densely populated Rochester 
and Syracuse MSAs, working-class markets with strong demand 
• Proximity to growing retail developments drives awareness, 
increases convenience for the consumer and attracts incremental 
traffic from bordering towns 
• Density of Splash express sites caters to the needs of a customer 
base that values convenience, speed and wash quality 
• Competitors typically lack the level of customer care that Splash is 
known for in the market 
• Splash is in the process of expanding its Upstate New York 
regional network, with 12 locations in active development and 
2 acquisitions under LOI 
• Management has identified the underpenetrated and densely 
populated Buffalo and Albany MSAs as primary targets for 
near- and medium -term expansion

II METRO-NORTH REGIONAL OVERVIEW 
Market Strategy 
• The Metro -North network, one of the highest -income regions in 
the country, represents Splash's foundational market 
• Scarcity of suitable parcels, high real estate development costs 
and complex permitting regulations provide exceptional 
barriers to entry 
• Splash locations are located along high -traffic areas, namely the 
1-95 corridor and the Merrit Parkway 
• In addition to express tunnel formats, Splash offers premium 
services like hand washes, detailing and late-night washes to a 
customer base that demands these services, capturing a greater 
share of consumer wallet and total market demand 
• Splash's membership network represents a significant competitive 
advantage and key differentiator, leveraging an extremely loyal 
customer base 
• Management is focused on increasing market density in attractive 
MSAs, including 5+ identified development sites expected to (tun 
over the next twelve months

I TRANSACTION OVERVIEW 
Ownership and 
Structure 
to rM „ 
r  17C.AVAS14 
• Splash is owned by Palladin Consumer Retail Partners, the original Splashfounders and select 
members of management the Company's operations are conducted through several wholly owned 
subsidiaries 
• The shareholders are exploring a sale of Splash in order to realize a return and to provide capital 
support for the next phase of the Company's organic and acquisition growth 
• The management team is committed to leading the expansion of the Splash platform and is excited 
about the Company's growth initiatives and the opportunity to invest alongside a new partner 
• An ideal partner will value the Company's existing sites and operations, add strategic value and 
support the numerous organic growth opportunities identified by management and provide dedicated 
resources and expertise to help execute Splash's acquisition and greenfield strategy 
• As of June 30, 2022, Splash owns the real estate for 16 operating sites and 6 development sites through 
wholly -owned subsidiaries that are expected to be included as part of the transaction 
• The transaction will be structured as a sale of stock 
Communications 
STRICTLY CONFIDENTIAL 
• The Company has retained BlackArch Partners LLC ("BlackArch") as its lead financial advisor, and 
William Blair & Company, LLC ("William Blair") as its co-advisor, to assist in discussions regarding 
the potential sale of Splash 
• As set forth in more detail in the confidentiality agreement delivered to BlackArch (i) the information 
contained in this Presentation is to be used by prospective buyers solely to aid in their evaluation of the 
potential purchase of the Company and (ii) under no circumstances should any officer, director, 
employee, independent contractor, consultant, customer, supplier or affiliate of Splash be contacted 
regarding this matter without the prior written approval of BlackArch

been engaged as its co-advisor, to assist in the proposed transaction.

investigation and analysis of Splash and does not purport to contain all of the information that may be required to evaluate the 
Company. In all cases, interested parties should conduct their own independent, in-depth investigation and analysis

prospective buyer of all or any portion of Splash. BlackArch has not independently verified any of the information, including any 
approximations, estimates or projections, contained herein and does not undertake any obligation to independently verify any 
other written or oral communication transmitted or made available to a prospective buyer of all or any portion of Splash.

representation or warranty (expressed or implied) as to the accuracy or completeness of the information contained in this 
Presentation or any other written or oral communication transmitted or made available to a prospective buyer of all or any portion 
of Splash; none of the Company, BlackArch or any of their respective affiliates or representatives shall have, and they expressly 
disclaim, any and all liability for, or based in whole or in part on, such information or other written or oral communication 
(including without limitation any expressed or implied representations), errors therein or omissions therefrom. Only those

agreement, when, as and if it is executed, and subject to such limitations and restrictions as may be specified in such definitive 
agreement, shall have legal effect.

delivery to any prospective buyer shall constitute an offer to sell or the solicitation of an offer to buy any assets or equity interest of 
Splash, nor shall this Presentation be construed to indicate that there has been no change in the affairs of Splash since the date 
hereof. The Company also reserves the right to terminate, at any time, the solicitation of indications of interest for Splash or the 
further participation in the investigation and proposal process by any party. Finally, the Company and BlackArch reserve the right 
to modify, at any time, any procedures related to such process without assigning any reason therefor. The Company intends to 
conduct business in the ordinary manner during the evaluation and offer period; however, the Company reserves the right to take 
any action, whether in or out of the ordinary course of business, including, but not limited to, the sale of property, which it deems 
necessary, prudent or desirable in the conduct of such business. 
All communications or inquiries relating to Splash should be directed to BlackArch. No personnel of the Company should be 
contacted directly under any circumstances. 
NOTE: All financial results presented herein reflect the consolidated performance of the platform, unless otherwise noted, 
and have been adjusted for one-time, non -recurring and select pro forma adjustments as identified and supported by a 
third -party Quality of Earnings report; historical financials exclude  any normalization adjustment for the impact of COVID-19

Footprint overview 
Tidal Wave snapshot 
Overview 
~Tidal Wave Auto Spa ("Tidal Wave" or the "Company") is one 
of the largest conveyor car wash systems in the United States, 
with a growing footprint of 50+ units primarily located across 
the Southeast. 
~As of September 2020, the system is composed of 46 express 
conveyor and 7 flex washes with 8 additional units expected to 
open before the end of the year 
~The platform has been growing at 50% + driven by its 
innovative experience, high quality service, footprint of premier 
site locations andizab1epipeline of units in development

PROJECTED FREE CASH FLOW SUMMARY 
Free cash flow commentary 
• Maintenance capital expenditures primarily consist of facility If ;IF y ,d the replacement of equipment 
• Maintenance capex is assumed to be 0.6% of sales in the projected period, in line with historical trends 
• As a result of low maintenance expenditure requirements, Soapy Joe's generates strong free cash flow conversion, averaging approximately 99% 
• Attractive acquisition profiles, with SLB dynamics to lessen the Cash requirements needed to fund investments in the forecast 
• Through 2026, management projects total spend of -$203M on construction and acquisition costs

EMPLOYEE SUMMARY 
Soapy Joe's employee life cycle 
• The Soapy Joe's employee life cycle was developed to provide top -tier customer 
service coaching via the following: 
• Onboarding 
- Introducing employees to Soapy Joe's steps of service E-learning module 
• Employee development 
- Via the 16-week Manger In Training (MIT) Program, the Company has created a 
great people leader pipeline that trains employees on subject matter ranging 
from HR Compliance to Membership Experience and developing an 
entrepreneurial mindset 
• Rewards and recognition 
- "Magic Moments" initiative over Microsoft Teams enables employees to recognize 
fellow team members for accomplishments 
• Performance management 
- Formal training and support processes and performance KPIs in place 
Approach to training: Blended learning 
Al Soapy Joe's. teams focus on a blended learning approach that bock 
efficiency, builds engagement, and creates a culture of feedback 
Learning Modalities 
• Award winning E-learning modules with gamification and k -ritoWlcie assessments 
• 30-60-90 onboarding plans and checklists 
• Ongoing Learning activities and check-in's 
• Instructor led training focused on continuous growth 
• LMS system on demand training that covers topics such as: Competency building, 
Leadership, safety, diversity, and compliance

SOAPY JOE'S IS A LEADER IN THE DEVELOPMENT OF 
SUSTAINABLE CAR WASH PRACTICES 
Soapy Joe's eco-friendly initiatives... 
Washing at Soapy Joe's saves 805 water vs. washing at home. Soapy Joe's holds 
the Water Savers designation from the International Car Wash Association. 
Reclaimed clarifier -water processes put Soapy Joe's ahead of the 
competition in water reclamation efforts and ongoing site -level 
improvements. 
Extensive engagement with environmental groups in the form of cash 
donations, in -kind donations, paid and earned media exposure to build 
community. 
Innovative roof -top gardens in exploration -phase with UCSD engineering 
students, which serve multiple purposes including building insulation and CO2 
offset 
Industry -first corn -based wrappers used for air freshener pockets to eliminate 
plastics. Further efforts include upcoming natural -latex string to replace plastic. -
based elastic. 
Soapy Joe's goes beyond industry standard equipment, replacing alt -the -
shelf nozzles in the tunnel with a low -flow, high-pressure alternative Mcnntoining 
wash quality. 
Soaps are pH balanced at the site -level and are biodegradable, which 
help ensure water that reaches the city sewer system is neutralized. 
Centralized thermostat controls at site -level keep employees comfortable. and 
energy use consistent and on -plan. LED lights used throughout the system to 
contribute to energy savings. 
...have led to the development of its low consumption express car wash system

Introduction 
Super Star is a leading player in the express car wash industry in the United States. The Company's stellar financial 
results and meteoric growth are fueled by a corporate organization that excels in the areas of operations, site selection 
and development, marketing, human resources, and financial controls.

Exetutive Summary p, _-,__ , Company Snapshot 
Super Star Car Wash ("Super Star" or "the Company") is the operator of one of the pre-eminent car 
wash chains in several of the hottest markets in the US. Founded in 1993, the Company has grown to 
33 sites, each exhibiting strong financial results and growth potential. With over two decades of 
operational experience, Management has positioned the Company to be one of the most profitable 
and recognized names in the markets it serves. 
The vast majority of the Company's locations are Express Wash only, while a small number of Full 
Service sites have been strategically located to serve a broad range of Super Star customers looking 
for enhanced service offerings. Express Wash represented roughly 90% of car wash revenue in 2021 
LTM through May (Full Service represented 10%). The Company benefits from recurring monthly 
members under its "Fast Pass" system, which has been growing sizably under Management's 
strategic guidance and represented 59% of car wash revenue in the LTM period. Sites utilize state-of-
the-art tunnels and washing equipment paired with courteous and reliable customer service, 
establishing the Company's reputation as one of the top wash providers in the US. 
Prospects for additional growth remain vibrant, both in terms of new locations and customer 
acquisition at current facilities. To further expand market share, the Company continues to identify 
suitable land and develop additional sites. Super Star's operational excellence along with its strong 
branding will allow the business to continue outperforming competitors in the markets of Phoenix, 
San Diego, and California's Inland Empire, as well as new markets it enters including Denver.

Contemplated Transaction 
b Represents 80 currently seeped sites only, before additional sites. 
Super Star Car Wash presents one of the few opportunities to acquire a Top 20 national chain and a high quality leader in the burgeoning car wash market. 
Management sees significant growth opportunities available for Super Star Car Wash, many of which are achievable given the current level of operation and 
some of which will benefit from the addition of an investor who can infuse additional resources toward their realization. Management is therefore looking for 
an acquirer who can provide capital and expertise to support the Company's promising trajectory. 
Strictly Private and Confidential 7 
Growth Opportunities 
Industry Trends 
The car wash sector has seen accelerated growth in recent years, particularly in Super Star's current markets. 
The advent of express car washes, wherein customers often purchase monthly memberships for the 
convenience of in-and-out access to automated wash tunnels, opened up the industry to a wider 
demographic. Those who were previously less concerned about a clean vehicle, or simply did not want to 
bear the time burden of waiting for a full service wash, continue to provide growth due to the speed, 
convenience, and value provided by express washes. Profitability is positively trending in the local market, 
with many key players increasing prices and therefore, revenue per car. 
Growth Opportunities 
Organic Growth 
Super Star's current markets of Phoenix, San Diego, and the Inland Empire continue to grow rapidly, 
prompting continued development and metropolitan expansion. As the amount of traffic, number of drivers, 
and consumer interest in express wash grows, volume is expected to increase. In addition, many operators 
including Super Star have recently increased wash prices with little to no adverse effect on demand. These 
twin opportunities in volume and value should contribute materially to Super Star's organic growth. 
Newer Technology 
Management continuously explores various new technologies aimed at increasing revenue and reducing costs while improving the customer experience. One 
of these technology improvements is the license plate recognition camera, for cars entering the wash lane. Among other benefits, the license plate 
recognition camera system prevents Fast Pass members from cancelling their current plans and re-enrolling during a promotional period, since the cameras 
would recognize the license plate (and member) as being already in the system. 
In addition to tracking Fast Pass customers, the camera system allows tracking of repeat non-member customers, providing the opportunity to upsell a given 
customer to a membership plan or a superior wash (eg, via one-time discount) based on their historical purchase patterns. These cameras cost approximately 
$10k per lane, along with annual support fees anticipated to be $3k per lane. Installing the cameras will also save the Company $0.90 per REID tag (usually 
purchased in batches of 50,000). Cameras are slated to be installed across all sites beginning in June 2021. In addition to this initiative, Management is 
exploring other opportunities to enhance retention and profitability, including methods to mitigate expiring credit card-related membership loss. 
Strictly Private and Confidential 3 
Growth Opportunities cont. 
New Development Sites 
Management has identified 47 sites, each of which is in various stages of 
development. All sites will be express car wash locations, and 12 are expected 
to open in late 2021 / early 2022 (with exact opening date predicated on 
construction and development timing). 31 of the locations are anticipated to 
include real estate, while the remaining 16 would be leased. At maturity, these 
development sites are expected to add approximately $76.8 mm to total 
EBITDA based on Management's projections. 
Note that, in addition to these opportunities, Management continually reviews 
a carefully selected pipeline of prospective sites for additional market share 
growth, and at the time of a contemplated transaction the list of development 
sites could include those outlined in this memorandum and/or a number of 
other locations. 
Mobile App 
Super Star was the first car wash company to develop a membership app in 
Collaboration with household name car wash vendor DRB Systems. The mobile 
app allows customers •to purchase washes, earn and redeem points, view 
current deals and find Super Star locations near them. Currently, over 58,000 
customers take advantage of the mobile app. The Company is currently 
undergoing a complete redesign of its website to enhance the customer online 
shopping experience with an expected mid June launch; upon completion of 
the website redesign, the mobile app will undergo a refresh as well.

Strictly Private and Confidential 9 
Investment Considerations 
A number of characteristics differentiate Super Star from other operators in the market, and it begins with Management's focus 
on providing the best car wash available, bar none. Key investment considerations also include: 
Brand and 
Reputation / 
Through years of operational excellence and consistent marketing efforts, Management has positioned Super Star as one of the 
most recognized and respected car wash brands in the markets it serves. This distinction has allowed the Company to build 
customer loyalty and credibility, helping facilitate site openings in untapped areas, increased service offerings, and price adjustments. 
Membership and 
Business Grewth 
Superior \ 
Developmept 
Capabilities 
Super Star's strong and growing monthly membership base is impressive. With 189,846 paying subscribers as of mid-June 2021, 
the Company accomplished an imposing 34.1% increase over December 2020's membership count alone. Growth in membership 
supplements the already notable organic growth in business, which in turn is amplified by growth through the Company's superior 
site development. 
Site selection and development is a core Super Star strength, cultivated over years of industry experience. A proven methodology 
for site selection based on specific metrics refined over years in the industry lays the groundwork, with only top sites pursued. 
Adding to this superior predictor system is a seasoned site development team well versed in bringing greenfield sites from 
surveying to permitting and from construction design to certificate of occupancy. This rarely matched combination of capabilities 
will support Super Star's profitable growth for years ahead. 
Operational 
Excellence , 
From superior equipment and technology to premium customer service, Super Star does not cut corners. Sites utilize the latest in 
Sonny's or MacNeil brand car wash equipment for an effective wash, while engaging in a proactive maintenance schedule. Not 
content with maintaining the status quo, Management is rolling out license recognition cameras in summer 2021 to further 
improve the car wash experience. To ensure premium customer experiences, the Company engages in secret shopper programs 
and customer satisfaction surveys, and daily staff requirements include periodic checks of all equipment at every site for optimal 
functionality. 
Strong \- Leadership Team 
Superior 
Marketing s5 
Super Star is led by a tenured management team focused on streamlining daily internal and external functions. The corporate 
office continues to gain sophistication alongside the operating business, including the hire in recent years of an experienced CFO, 
Controller, HR Director, IT team, and Sales & Marketing Director, as well as various junior staff, multiplying the capabilities of the 
business. 
Super Star dedicates considerable attention and resources to marketing strategy. The Company has excelled at outreach, with 
promotions across traditional and digital platforms. Its mobile app, text marketing, and social media presence are particularly 
noteworthy, complemented by community partnerships that foster customer loyalty. A large following has developed as a result of these 
efforts, with over 213,000 text subscribers, 375,000 email subscribers, 14,000 Facebook followers, and 8,600 Instagram followers.

Evolution of the Business 
Super Star has evolved across site selection, site opening, and operations spheres 
• The Company is more streamlined and professional now than ever, with a strong corporate office ready for the next stage of operation 
• Operations have become sophisticated 
— The time to secure Fast Pass customers is quicker 
— New site operations — with the advent of the dedicated Opening Team — has created smooth, faster-ramp openings with strong training and hiring 
• Economies of scale have taken hold, combined with Management's industry leading site selection methodology 
• The Company enjoys proper size, power, and experience, with resources to put to new sites 
• Management has built a trajectory that takes Super Star beyond just its current sites, and readies the brand for its next stage 
Strictly Private and Confidential 12 
Company History 
The first Super Star site was opened in 1993 by Reza Amirrezvani, with growth continuing through April 2021 to 33 active sites, as well as eight other sites 
that were built and later sold. Initially, all sites were full service until 2009, when the market shifted towards express washes in favor of their higher margins 
and wider consumer acceptance. Since that time, all existing full service washes have been converted to include express lanes, and all recent builds have 
been constructed as pure express washes, with the exception of 19th and Baseline and Higley locations.

Strictly Private and Confidential 14 
„ Company Overview 
Fast Pass Membership Program 
Overview 
Super Star's customers can broadly be segmented as either Fast Pass members or pay-
per-use non-members. Members are charged on a monthly basis based on a package 
of their choosing. There are various plans for both express and full service washes, and 
program prices range from $17.95 to $59.95 per month in Arizona, and $22.95 to 
$34.95 per month in California. 
Membership Growth 
The Company prides itself on its Fast Pass unlimited plans. Indeed, it's Super Star's 
trademark: "We Do Unlimited Right,” with the Company offering a range of 
membership programs across service levels. Super Star's approach to the market, in 
which the benefits of saving time and money are promoted alongside the ability to 
cancel anytime, has helped underscore the strong growth in memberships in recent 
years. Of the 6.9 million cars to have visited a Super Star site in 2021 LTM through 
May, 60% were Fast Pass members. Membership revenue reached $36.8 mm and 
accounted for =59% of all car wash sales. 
Through its strong Fast Pass focus, creative marketing, and customer incentives, Super 
Star has been able to consistently grow its membership enrollment rate, resulting in 
notable net growth each year. As of May 2021, Super Star's membership base 
increased to 186,540 monthly subscribers, which grew further to 189,846 as of mid-
June 2021. 
In addition to the benefits of membership provided to Super Star customers, the 
Company also benefits from its growing ranks of Fast Pass members, with the 
recurring revenue from memberships helping to smooth out the negative impacts of 
inclement weather and seasonality that afflict chains across the industry.

Strictly Private and Confidential 15 
Fast Pass Membership Program Cont. 
Strong Ramp in Membership 
Management's sharp focus on Fast Pass membership is evident in the metrics 
tracked by the Company. Car counts from Fast Pass members reached 60.1% of 
total car counts in the 2021 YTD period, up from 48.9% of car counts in 2019, and 
37.2% in 2017. As seen in the table "Average Months to Membership Milestones", 
the implementation of stronger membership sales programs over recent years has 
materially reduced the number of months it takes for the average site to get to the 
1,000 member threshold, 4,000 member threshold, and higher. While express sites 
historically took an average of 42 months to reach the 4,000 member level, sites 
opened in 2019-2020 through August took just 16 months on average.

Fleet Program 
In late 2020, Super Star launched a fleet program, bringing on a seasoned business 
account executive to develop fleet accounts. The Company is currently offering four 
programs, including prepaid accounts, fleet cards, monthly fleet plans, and house 
accounts; the Company has already added dozens of fleet customers since inception.

Strictly Private and Confidential 16 
Corporate Structure and Capabilities 
The Company is comprised of 33 currently operating car washes, each structured under a 
separate LLC with the exception of three locations — Warner Rd, 40th and Baseline, and 
Higley — which are combined under the entitySSCW 67° Ave LLC. In addition to these, there 
are 47 sites in development as of writing across Arizona, California, and Colorado. Each 
LLC has a different equity structure, with varying numbers of investors. Super Star founder 
Reza Amirrezvani is the majority stakeholder of each entity through his solely-owned 
entity, SS Enterprise Holdings, LLC., with majority interests ranging from 57% to 100%. 
Corporate Capabilities 
Super Star's tremendous growth and profitability have necessitated the addition of a 
number of corporate resources in support of a best-in-class car wash operation. These 
resources have subsequently allowed the Company to achieve superior results. This 
virtuous circle has fueled the success the Company has realized to date, but of equal 
importance it has positioned Super Star to continue its expansion going forward. 
Corporate capabilities have evolved to include: 
Financial Controls 
Marketing 
Operations 
Development 
The addition of an experienced corporate CFO and analyst to the 
finance and accounting function has streamlined reporting and 
made data available in time to impact critical decisions. 
Amortizing the cost of marketing over more sites has allowed 
Super Star to hire a seasoned marketing team that can reach 
more customers more effectively. 
The corporate team can focus resources on operational 
excellence. One example is a dedicated manager responsible for 
opening new washes, effectively applying lessons learned and 
dramatically reducing time to profitability of new sites. 
The development team can dedicate more time and focus on 
identifying promising geographies and sites, then overseeing 
entitlement and construction.

Strictly Private and Confidential 18 
Employees 
The Company employed 626 individuals as of May 2021 across operations, managerial, corporate, and 
administrative functions. Many of these are car wash associates (231 as of May, or 37% of total staff), 
followed by Fast Pass sales representatives, numbering 152 as of May and often the first faces a customer 
sees as they approach the car wash. Each employee goes through an E-Verify process prior to onboarding 
to ensure compliance with labor regulations. The Company provides full benefits to employees (health, 
dental, and life insurance, as well as 401k), which plays a crucial role in mitigating attrition. 
Training 
One of the key factors to Super Star's success is the superior staff training and discretionary incentives 
provided, which in Management's view allow the Company to maintain one of the highest employee 
retention rates in the industry. With training modules on various aspects of operations now available to 
staff via mobile device, the Company is better situated to keep employees informed and knowledgeable 
while cultivating enhanced employee involvement. 
In another step to further enhance the customer experience alongside employee development, Super Star 
is in the process of hiring several customer service field trainers. The role of these trainers will be to 
evaluate the customer experience at each site, including operations, sales, and service. The customer 
service field trainer will use carefully designed scorecards to guide evaluations for relaying to site leaders 
and team members areas of opportunity as well as excellence. These dedicated field trainer resources will 
add yet another point of differentiating value, not only for customers but also for employees who can 
create action plans for continuous development.

From its initial success as a founder-led enterprise, Super Star has grown its professional structure to meet the needs of a larger organization. Strong bench 
depth has been added in recent years across HR, finance, marketing, and development. Adding to this, directors of customer service and sales and marketing 
were recruited to drive further service focus and membership growth. Dedicated personnel have also been brought on focused exclusively on new location 
siting, acquisition, development, and construction, employing the multi-faceted site selection methodology perfected over years by Founder Reza Amirrezvani. 
With the size and capabilities of the current team, Super Star is poised for the next stage of growth through 2021-2022 development and beyond.

Leadership Team 
Reza Amirrezvani Founder 
Reza Amirrezvani is the Founder and CEO of Super Star Car Wash, which he started in 1993 when he opened the first location in Chandler, Arizona. Mr. 
Amirrezvani has built and operated 42 car washes altogether over the course of his career, having sold a number of them in the process. Today, he is 
actively involved in growing Super Star's operations by securing and building new sites, among other strategic initiatives. In addition to car washes, Mr. 
Amirrezvani has operated a portfolio of office complexes, retail centers, and other multi-tenant real estate projects, which have been sold. Prior to his 
ventures in real estate, he founded a telemarketing company in Colorado and San Diego, and worked for Grubb & Ellis in Phoenix. Mr. Amirrezvani 
attended the University of California, San Diego where he pursued a bachelor's degree in Economics. 
Dan Vaith Chief Financial Officer 
As CFO at Super Star, Dan Vaith has been responsible for transforming the corporate office. Since his arrival in April 2018, Mr. Vaith fostered the creation of 
the accounting department, as well as implemented technology and HR initiatives and improvements, including implementing an ERP / Accounting solution. 
He was responsible for shortening the month-end close, overall streamlining of processes and procedures, and improving operational and financial reporting 
through practices that align with long-term strategies. Most recently he introduced expanded analysis to the organization. Mr. Vaith brings over 25 years of 
experience in accounting and finance roles, including 15 years in leadership / management, having started his career as an insurance premium auditor 
before transitioning into corporate accounting / finance. He has completed MBA courses and earned the CPA designation, and received his bachelor's degree 
in Accounting from Metropolitan State University. 
1 
Scott Elgersma Chief Operating Officer 
Scott Elgersma is the Chief Operating Officer for Super Star, where he is tasked with overseeing five general managers, training employees, and maintaining 
morale. Prior to Super Star, Mr. Elgersma worked as a Service Advisor for Super Station Car Wash. He quickly became the top salesperson for the company 
and was promoted to Lead Trainer. In 1995, he left Super Station for Super Star and was promoted to General Manager, where he oversaw operations, sales, 
and maintenance. His excellence in that capacity led him to his latest promotion and current role. 
Jonathan Kierman Vice President of Sales and Marketing 
Jonathan Kierman is a sales, marketing, and operations executive with over 30 years of experience in the retail industry. As a customer-centric 
innovation leader, Mr. Kierman has worked for multiple national retail brands holding various leadership and executive roles including Famous 
Footwear, Roundy's Supermarkets, Ascena Retail Group, Vera Bradley and Jockey International. Prior to joining Super Star, Mr. Kierman worked as a 
strategy and marketing consultant helping a wide range of companies develop strategic marketing plans. He is a graduate of Arizona State University. 
Strictly Private and Confidential 21 
Leadership Team cont. 
Charmaine Brinegar Director of Human Resources 
Charmaine Brinegar is instrumental in restructuring FIR administration process flows and implementing HRIS systems, managing all aspects of the human 
resources area. Ms. Brinegar brings over 12 years of experience in human resource management and has worked in the fields of technology, banking, 
and education. She is nationally recognized as a Student Chapter President with SHRM and has earned her SHRM-CP designation. In addition, she is a 
PhD candidate in the field of Industrial-Organizational Psychology. 
Benjamin Durham Director of Information Technology 
Benjamin Durham joined the Company in August 2019 and has been expanding its technological footprint ever since. Mr. Durham started as the sole 
member of the IT team but quickly grew the department into five full time employees that deliver continuous operations support. With over 12 years of 
experience in the field, he carries a varied background in distribution, manufacturing, banking, and government. He is always looking to bring continuing 
efficiencies and automation to the car wash. Mr. Durham has a bachelor's degree in Computer Science. 
ITom Droste General Manager — Full Service Operations 
Tom Droste brings over 34 years of experience in the car wash industry including full service, express, and detail services. While completing a degree in CAD, 
Mr. Droste worked at a car wash and quickly realized the opportunities available in the car wash industry. As General Manager of full service operations, Mr. 
Droste oversees the day-to-day operations and is accountable for sales and labor performance, maintenance and staffing, and coaching/training of new hires 
at full service locations. 
IRuben Bugayong General Manager — Express Wash, West Valley Operations 
Ruben Bugayong joined the Super Star team in June 2010 and was one of Super Star's first fast pass membership salesmen. Transitioning to management, 
Mr. Bugayong opened Super Star's first two express locations before shifting to management of full service stores where he led, trained, and coached teams 
for eight years. He was eventually promoted to Express General Manager for Arizona West Valley locations in June 2018 and now oversees operations across 
seven express sites, where he is accountable for sales and labor performance, maintenance and staffing, and coaching/training of new hires. 
IDennis Schackelford General Manager — Express Wash, East Valley Operations 
Dennis Shackelford joined Superstar in 2017 as a Fast Pass sales representative and climbed quickly through the ranks with a friendly, team player attitude. 
As general manager of Arizona East Valley operations, Mr. Shackelford oversees the day to day operations of six express locations and is accountable for 
sales, labor performance, staffing / coaching, and training new hires at those locations.

Leadership Team cont. 
111 William Caley General Manager — Convenience Store Operations 
Joining Super Star in January 2021, William is responsible for maximizing opportunities within multi-unit Super Star convenience store retail operations. 
William is an industry expert with 15 years of experience, excited to bring a new perspective to Super Star. A servant leader, William's goals are achieved by 
putting others' needs first. William's duties include continuous process improvements, management development, vendor relations, price book 
management, contract negotiations, image, asset protection, sales, and most importantly, guest experiences. 
Brice Sack General Manager — Express and New Sites 
Brice Sack holds 21 years of car wash and oil & lube experience. Brice originally came over to the Super Star team in 2017. In 2018, he opened one of Super 
Star's new express sites, a location which later would become a Company training site. Brice has leveraged his management and car wash experience to 
coach and train several new managers. In November 2019, Brice became an express general manager. Brice has opened three new express locations for 
Super Star, and has been given the lead on opening new future sites. 
JR Ruelas Director of Quality Control and Consultant 
JR Ruelas has been in the car wash industry as a manager and partner for over 48 years, having began his career in Central California and subsequently being 
recruited by larger organizations. He has managed multiple locations both full service and express, and was awarded Manager of the Year by the Western 
Car Wash Association. Mr. Ruelas has had particular success in membership plan marketing. For 10 years prior to coming to Super Star, he worked at Cobblestone 
Auto Spa where he helped grow the organization from two locations to ten. He currently an Operations Manager and Partner at Super Star Car Wash in 
Phoenix and helped grow and manage Super Star locations from five sites to over 30. He graduated Fresno City College and attended Fresno State University. 
Ross Liebler District General Manager — California Operations 
Ross Liebler has been with Super Star for nearly eight years, having started as an express location manager. During his tenure he was promoted to General 
Manager for the Company's California sites, and was recently promoted again to California District GM after contributing significantly to expanding 
operations in that state. Mr. Uebler's prior experience includes 19 years with Foot Locker where he was a store manager and manager trainer, in addition to 
having held manager positions with Finish Line and Dollar General.

Legal, Environmental and Safety 
Legal 
The Company has not been involved in, is not currently involved in, and does not 
anticipate any litigation or other legal issues of a material nature, with the exception of one 
recent allegation: Super Star was recently named in a California employment case by a 
former employee alleging he should have been categorized as a full time employee. 
While the Company believes it is not at fault, the parties are in the process of pursuing 
a settlement, and Management anticipates the maximum amount of exposure to be $125k. 
Environmental 
The Company is compliant with all resource and environmental regulations and 
Management does not have knowledge of any issues past, current, or pending. 
Safety 
In recent history the Company has not experienced any material worker's 
compensation claims or safety concerns, with no material OSHA violations. The 
Company's Experience Modification Rate (EMOD) for Arizona stands at 0.72, while the 
Company's EMOD rate for California stands at 0.60, reflecting the comparatively safer 
record at Super Star compared to the industry average. 
Suppliers 
Each Super Star site uses a unique mix of suppliers suited for their respective 
operations. Terms are Net 30 for most suppliers except for the Company's fuel 
vendors, which are paid on receipt, and its largest vendor, Carwash Services, which is 
Net 60. The latter is responsible for sourcing equipment, chemicals, maintenance, and 
installation, among other car wash-related needs. For locations with fuel, three sites 
are branded with Chevron fuel; one site with Shell. The table seen here details the 
Company's top 10 suppliers, of 29 suppliers in total.

Marketing and Promotions 
A key differentiator between Super Star and the competition is the use of a 
comprehensive marketing strategy which allows the Company to reach a wide audience. 
Radio 
Super Star partners from time to time with top local news stations as a weather and traffic sponsor. As 
part of this media partnership, the Company is allotted up to 30 seconds per commercial airing an 
average of eight times a day. Radio advertisements are strategically timed during rush hours in the 
morning and afternoons to capture customers driving to and from work. This media channel is ideal for 
announcing promotions or giveaways. 
In the Phoenix market, Super Star has developed four key radio partnerships: Riviera Broadcasting, 
Audacy (formerly Bonneville), Entercomm, and Hubbard. With Riviera Broadcasting, the Company 
continues its long-standing relationship as the Exclusive Traffic Sponsor for three popular local stations. 
The Company partnered with Audacy in 2021 to air 24 spots per week on one of the top country radio 
stations in the market, reaching over 600,000 listeners per month. Also in 2021, Super Star added 
advertising on one of the most listened to sports radio stations in the metro area with a total of 80 
overall ad spots, reaching over 223,000 listeners per week and an online streaming platform reaching 
over 500,000 listeners per month. With Hubbard, one of Phoenix's premier rock stations is partnering 
with Super Star on two spotlight events in 2021 involving significant Super Star promotion through on-
air promotions, e-blasts to 50,000+ listeners, Facebook posts to 99,000+ followers, and Live Remotes 
at Super Star locations. Additional details about the Company's strong multi-faceted radio marketing 
can be made available. 
Digital Radio 
In California, Super Star has embarked on a digital radio campaign with 'Heart Media directly targeting 
consumers by identifying zip codes within a 10-mile radius of its locations, with 30 second spots 
reaching approximately 240,000 potential customers each month. Additional services provided by 
iHeart include utilizing geofence targeting which serves banner ads to mobile device users within a 5-
mile radius of locations; this targeting reaches over 159,000 'Heart listeners per month.

AZFamily The company is a sponsor for AZFamily's KTVK Channel 3 and KPHO CBS news stations,

advertisements are typically placed in the morning during weather segments to capture customers

the partnership, Cox airs the weekly High School Football Game of the Week in which Super Star 
Car Wash will be the sponsor of the Super Star Player of the Game.

Marketing and Promotions cont. 
Text Messaging 
With a deep text message file of over 213,000 subscribers, in partnership with OptSpot (a leading car wash text messaging 
provider) Super Star has developed an industry leading text drip campaign aimed at three audiences: a) current Fast Pass 
members, b) Fast Pass members not actively using their plan, and c) customers that are not Fast Pass members. Each 
campaign is designed to encourage usage, promote upgrades of plans, and — in the case of non-member customers — drive 
Fast Pass enrollments. The Company also utilizes a bi-weekly text message with promotions and deals for customers to 
use a variety of services including detailing and oil & lube (at Arizona full service locations). 
Digital Marketing 
The company embarked on a relationship with Welcomemat Services (a leader in digital marketing with deep industry 
knowledge) in late 2020 on targeted digital campaigns. With four pilot locations in Arizona, Welcomemat utilized its 
Perfect Match digital ads to target customers with a propensity for washing their car. The acquired customers are served a 
retargeting ad with an offer for an unlimited plan (express) or detail ad (full service). As a result of the pilot program, the 
Company recently launched to all six full service locations and to date has acquired over 4,800 customers, equating to an 
ROI of over $122,000. 
Super Star recently added a Digital Marketing Manager to the team, tasked with developing ongoing digital strategies, 
improving SEO/SEM presence for each location as well as the Company brand overall, and targeting customers with 
compelling marketing to drive traffic to the website and physical sites. 
Billboards 
For a more traditional approach, from time to time Super Star employs the use of billboards to attract potential 
customers. As part of a larger branding initiative in California, the Company recently placed a 15'x49' billboard along one 
of the most traveled San Diego area roads (Highway 78) to build brand awareness. 
Direct Mail 
Another traditional route, the Company uses targeted direct mail to gain new customers. Mailers typically coincide with 
grand opening and are sent to car owners in targeted zip codes nearby. On average, 30,000 postcards with free washes 
are sent per new site, with a redemption rate of approximately 7.8%.

Super Star is the first major car wash chain to develop a mobile app with industry leader DRB

Social Media 
In the rapidly changing landscape of social media, the Company has kept pace with the consumer 
by tailoring its messaging in order to resonate. Transitioning from giveaways and contests to a 
more holistic approach, the Company has constructed a strategic social media calendar to engage 
followers through car wash education, promotions, employee and community recognition, and 
human interest. Facebook followers exceed 14,000, Instagram followers exceed 8,600, and the 
Company recently launched digital targeting to grow its YouTube following. Super Star is also 
exploring the use of influencers in mediums such as Tik Tok along with lnstagram and Facebook. 
Community Partnerships 
The Company strategically partners with various corporations, charities, businesses and first 
responders in Arizona and California. It also is a proud sponsor of various local schools and youth 
activity groups. In doing so, Super Star is able to create personal relationships within the 
community and increase brand awareness while giving back. This year, Super Star is engaging in 
major partnerships with Phoenix Children's Hospital to sponsor Child Car Seat Safety Week, as well 
as with Paul's Car Wash to support Big Brothers/Big Sisters of Arizona and KUPD to provide 
resources to 1,000 of Arizona's deployed troops.

marketing plan. One such opportunity arose recently with the Arizona Republic, the state's flagship

Operations Overview 
Overview 
The Company operates 26 car wash sites opened in 2019 or before, opened 7 sites in 
2020-2021, and is in various stages of building 47 development sites. With the exception 
of a handful of older locations, most sites operate with three pay stations allowing for 
more fluid traffic, and conveyor lengths at Super Star sites range from 95 to 160 ft  (while 
most sites fall within 120-155 ft). While Management has certainly built and refined the 
model as it pertains to express car wash operations, the keys to Super Star's market 
success are more than what can be drawn on a blueprint. 
Keys to Success 
Super Star's success starts and finishes with providing customers with the best car wash 
available: 
• Company staff as the real "Super Stars" 
— Excellence-focused culture methodically developed and maintained 
— Healthy competition both internal and external 
— Market-leading retention 
— Extensive training 
Performance metrics drive sales, profits, and employee incentives 
• Fanatical focus on customer service 
• State-of-the-art, well-maintained equipment 
Land Leases 
The land at most Super Star sites is owned, however several locations operate under 20-
year land leases. Leases generally have the option to extend five years for four periods. 
Note the Company recently undertook sale-leaseback transactions at Greenfield, 
Northern, and 40th and Baseline sites. Management is currently negotiating four 
additional sale-leasebacks; if ultimately closed, these would impact EBITDA by an 
estimated =1.0 mm. In addition to the locations presented here, Super Star also leases 
offices at 1830 N. 95th Ave in Phoenix for corporate purposes.

Strictly Private and Confidential 40 
Development Sites - Methodical Selection 
Overview 
Each Super Star site goes through a rigorous, objective grading system. This 
approach has been refined over time to reflect successes and challenges and is now 
a highly reliable predictor of car wash performance. 
Grading Criteria 
Management's site selection rubric for determining whether to pursue a particular 
location for express car wash development involves a number of factors, each of 
which is graded on a proprietary, specific set of quantitative and qualitative 
measurements. A few of these criteria are as follows: 
• Area Profile — Including shopping, business, residential, and industrial 
considerations 
• Competitor Proximity — With reflection on competition in the same traffic 
pattern as well as proximity of competitors overall 
• Lot Specifics — Whether a lot is corner or otherwise located; traffic light presence 
• Site Accessibility — Ease of ingress, egress from both traffic directions 
• Entrance Stacking — How many cars the location's lot dimensions will readily 
allow at the wash entrance 
• Traffic Counts — With consideration to both destination point and commuter 
traffic patterns 
• Demographics — Ranking sites by number of households within a certain radius, 
comparative median household affluence, population age 
In addition to these, there are five other criteria that are assessed and scored. An 
illustrative example of the grading scorecard used by Management is seen here, 
representing actual candidate sites that have been reviewed in recent years. This 
methodology to new site selection, developed through years of operational and 
development experience, assists in the independent analysis of sites that will aid and 
support Super Star's profitable growth for years ahead.

Development Sites - Select Locations 
One of Super Star's core strengths lies in its site selection methodology, cultivated over years of car wash development and operation. This methodology is 
based on a refined set of specific criteria for area profile, competition, accessibility, lot dynamics, traffic counts, and key demographics, among other 
elements. Each criterion is scored and totaled for an overall grade (B, B+, A-, A), and only top sites are pursued. Below is a selection of sites being pursued for 
estimated completion by end of 2021 (among others slated for opening in 2021 / 2022): 
Happy Valley and 35t1i (Phoenix, AZ) Located in a center with high volume tenants (QT, Dutch Bros, Starbucks), this location has strong destination point 
traffic (over 35k vehicles per day, or VPD) as well as internal traffic pattern maneuvering, with great visibility and access. With high median income 
demographics to generate strong dollars per car, this site scored an A in Super Star's site selection process (overleaf), and Management anticipates this site 
will quickly reach $2 mm EBITDA. 
59th Ave and Thunderbird (Glendale, AZ) Surrounded by over 600k sq ft of Class A and B shops, restaurants, and offices, including high-volume tenants (Fry's 
Grocery, Chick Fil-A, Starbucks), the location has destination point traffic with over 35k VPD and notable internal traffic pattern maneuvering for high volume. 
With strong median income demographics, visibility, and access, this site also earned an A score and is expected to rapidly reach over $2 mm EBITDA. 
Scottsdale Rd (Scottsdale, AZ) Located in one of the most sought-after locations in downtown Scottsdale, in an area undergoing major revitalization 
(15,000+ apartment units being constructed), there is excellent traffic at this site (over 42k VPD), good visibility and access, and high median income 
demographics. The site scored an A- and is expected to approach $2 mm EBITDA quickly. 
Mission Ave (Oceanside, CA) Pulling from a large right-fit demographic area with no competition for miles, this site will sit next to a new 7-Eleven c-store / 
gas station. Great visibility, with high traffic counts both on nearby Highway 76 (65k VPD) and Mission/Foussat (over 30k VPD). Noteworthy for San Diego, the 
site will feature a 145 ft tunnel and 42 vacuums. With high median income demographics, the site scored a high A- and should quickly approach $2 mm EBITDA. 
Mission Center (San Diego, CA) Generating one of the highest grades in Super Star's scoring process, this site is located on a main connecting road with 30k 
VPD in highly desirable Mission Valley. Surrounded by over 2 million sq ft of Class A and B shops, restaurants, and offices, it has strong visibility and access, and 
will benefit from a dense median income population. Featuring 35 vacuums and a 135 ft tunnel, notable for San Diego, over $2 mm in EBITDA is expected quickly. 
Falcon (Falcon, CO) Located on a main connector road with strong destination point traffic (30k VPD), visibility, and access, the location is situated in an 
extremely low vacancy area with few small retail spaces. In the heart of Falcon with 121 active new home communities, the site is well located at the 
entrance of a King Sooper shopping center in a trade area with good tenant mix, multiple national restaurants, Super Walmart, Safeway, and other notable 
retail. The site scored an A- and is anticipated to approach $2 mm EBITDA quickly. 
Sheridan (Denver, CO) Located at the main entrance of a high producing shopping area with great tenant mix (including King Sooper, Home Depot, multiple 
national restaurants, and other retail), the site has strong visibility and access as well as traffic counts (over 44k VPD). Densely populated with median income 
demographics, the site scored an A and is expected to rapidly approach $2 mm EBITDA.

Car Wash Industry 
Overview of US Market 
The car wash industry is broadly comprised of five main segments: express, in-bay 
automatics, detailing services, self-serve, and hand washes. The demand for express 
wash has increased over the past five years as rising per capita income levels enabled 
consumers to spend more on discretionary services, and the express wash segment 
is expected to continue to gain industry share. According to industry resource 
Professional Carwashing and Detailing, there are an estimated 28,500 express 
washes in the US, and Super Star is among the Top 20 chains in the nation. 
The car wash industry is impacted by several market forces, and factors that 
influence disposable income impact the sector. According to industry research house 
IBIS World, continued improvement in both per capita disposable income and 
households earning more than $100k is expected to increase demand for car wash 
services. From 2011 to 2020, IBISWorld estimates annual revenue increased 19.7%. 
However, amidst the pandemic in 2020, many state governments imposed the 
closure of businesses to slow the spread of the coronavirus. Furthermore, stay-at-
home orders diminished demand for industry services at locations that remained 
open. As a large number of individuals shifted to work and study from home, the 
wear-and-tear rate of vehicles declined, and so did demand for car wash as well as 
peripheral services like auto detailing. Due to the aforementioned factors, industry 
revenue dropped 13.6% from 2019 to 2020. (Note, through the difficulties 
associated with Covid-19, Super Star's business continued to grow.) Looking forward, 
over the next five years to 2025, industry revenue is forecasted to rise at a CAGR of 
3.4% to $12.9 billion. 
Total revenue for the car wash and detailing industry has increased significantly since 
2009. In addition to the rise in per capita disposable income, industry performance 
has benefited from downward trends in oil and gas prices, particularly in 2015 and 
2016. However, as the economy has continued to improve, fuel prices have 
rebounded somewhat, causing revenue growth to decelerate in response. 
Nevertheless, industry revenues are expected to rise 5.3% by the end of 2021.

Car Wash Industry cont. 
Motor Vehicle Registrations 
Growth in car wash revenue can be tied to the number of registered vehicles in the 
US. Over the past five years, the amount of motor vehicle registrations has grown at 
an annualized rate of 0.43%. Generally, when there are more vehicles registered for 
the road, the demand for car wash services increase. Vehicle registrations are 
expected to increase at a CAGR of 1.44% to 294.9 million by 2026. 
Per Capita Disposable Income 
As with many discretionary services, the car wash industry is closely tied to 
consumer disposable income. As the latter increases, the consumer's ability to pay 
for washes should increase as well. According to IBISWorld, economic indicators that 
drive disposable income levels are expected to steadily strengthen over the next five 
years as new tax policies are implemented and low unemployment rates prevail.

Financial Summary 
Income Statements 
Financial Statement Overview 
Super Star has exhibited strong income statement trends while 
maintaining a solid balance sheet foundation to further expand. 
The results seen here are summarized on a consolidated basis, 
with financials for the SS Holding and corporate entities 
combined with those of the Arizona and California sites. 
Day-to-day business is run on an accrual basis and financial 
reporting operates on a calendar year basis, with Microsoft 
Dynamics 365 used as the Company's accounting software. 
Historical financials have been reviewed by independent 
accountant BeachFleischman PC, and starting in 2020 the 
Company has tapped the same firm for audit services. 
Income Statement Summary 
The Company's income statements showcase strong top line 
and bottom line performance. Primary revenue generator Car 
Wash sales, which includes both membership revenues as well 
as pay-per-wash sales, experienced 32.6% growth between 
2019 and 2020, and a few months later, grew another 20.6% 
from 2020 to the 2021 LTM period through May. The only 
revenue line which has declined materially since 2019 is Fuel, a 
result of market gasoline prices, and which is not a significant 
profit center for the business. 
Note that beginning in March 2019, Management raised the 
base wash price from $3.00 to $5.00, and thus 2019 results 
reflect a mix of price points. Base washes are now up to $6.00 in 
Arizona, while in California the base pricing is $7.00 to $9.00. 
Even with these price increases the Company. is not losing 
volume, and anticipates further price increases in July 2021. In 
addition, through the difficulties associated with Covid-19, the 
business continued to grow.

Strictly Private and Confidential 47 
EBITDA Adjustments 
Four areas of adjustment were made to Super Star's 2021 LTM EBITDA. These adjustments include 
elimination of losses for newly opened sites, non-recurring legal fees, organization! transaction costs, 
and PPP proceeds booked to miscellaneous income. 
New Site Adjustments 
• New car wash sites tend to increase operating losses as they ramp up business 
• To eliminate the drag that new locations bring to overall profitability, negative LTM EBITDA 
amounts were eliminated for Linda Vista and Melrose locations 
Other Adjustments 
• The Company incurred legal expenses at its California sites in the 2021 LTM period of $75k, which 
were non-recurring in nature related to an employment matter 
• Super Star was involved in sale-leaseback transactions in the 2021 LTM period which incurred 
$268k and $175k in fees at two sites, Greenfield and 40th Ave, respectively. One-time organization 
structure costs were also incurred of $127k 
• In 2020 the Company applied for and received PPP (Paycheck Protection Program) loans through 
the SBA. The Company later successfully applied for loan forgiveness, which was booked in 
December 2020 to miscellaneous income ($515k). An adjustment has been made removing this 
additional income from EBITDA consideration 
Previous Year Adjustments 
In addition to adjustments similar in nature to the above, in 2019 and 2020 Income from Subsidiaries of 
$4.8 mm and $12.8 mm, respectively, were also excluded to arrive at EBITDA. These represent intercompany 
amounts consisting of Super Star net income allocated toss Holdings after allocations to other investors. 
Note on Corporate Allocations 
Each site (except for new sites with recent openings) is charged a management fee for corporate 
overhead. Overhead expenses include rent for the corporate facility, professional fees, and 
management salaries, and totaled -=$3.5 mm in 2021 LTM. Management anticipates corporate 
expenses as a % of consolidated revenue will decrease overtime, since current corporate levels should 
generally support overall operations for the near future.

Super Star operates with a high level of fixed assets (PP&E), valued at $129.3 mm 
net of depreciation as of May 2021. Buildings represents the largest category, at 
$76.7 mm for the period, before depreciation. The Company's current asset 
balance is dominated by Cash of $18.0 mm, as well as Assets in Progress of $7.4 
mm related to new development activity. 
Capital Expenditures

primarily comprised of buildings and land, but also car wash equipment, 
computers, and other PP&E associated with new builds being undertaken. Note 
land value was also adjusted for a sale-leaseback undertaken by the Company at 
their 40th Ave site. Management anticipates additional levels of capital 
investment in the latter part of 2021 and in 2022 correlated with the Company's 
continued expansion via new builds (referencing information provided above on 
development site costs).

Balance Sheet Discussion 
Current Assets 
Current Assets as of May 2021 totaled =26.9 mm. After Cash, Assets in 
Progress and Inventory round off the top three accounts. Other Current 
Assets include prepaid expenses, occasional amounts due from affiliates, 
and Accounts Receivable. As with other businesses in the car wash sector, 
Accounts Receivable plays a minimal role in working capital, totaling just $19k. 
Inventory is counted on an annual basis and totaled 41.3 mm as of May 
2021. Neo Inventory represented the largest category at $302k and consists 
of inventory held in convenience and lube stores. Micro Fiber Towels and 
Fuel are the next largest items at $208k and $187k, respectively. Chemicals 
and other consumables can also be found within the Inventory total, as well 
as parts for wash tunnels and other areas of operation. 
Current Liabilities 
Current Liabilities as of May 2021 totaled 47.7 mm. Accrued Expenses 
represented the largest account at 43.5 mm, consisting of Accrued Payroll, 
Accrued Utilities, Accrued Car Wash Supplies/Payables, and other items. 
Deferred Revenue and Accounts Payable, totaling 42.3 mm and =$1.8 mm 
respectively, make up the second and third largest Current Liabilities 
categories. 
The Company generally pays A/P on a timely basis, as evidenced by the A/P 
Aging table seen here. Note the four largest accounts are associated with 
current construction and development efforts, and don't constitute 
payables associated with the normal operating business: AP Global, DRB 
Systems, Cawley Architects, and Architecture Orange.
