About Hoffman Car Wash 
ransactions 
Founded in 1965, Hoffman Car Wash ("HCW" or the "Company"), led by industry veteran Tom Hoffman Jr., is a 
top fifty (50) conveyor chain in the US and is located in New York's Capital Region, the Adirondacks, Hudson Valley and 
Southern Tier. A multi-generational family-run business, HCW has grown to include twenty-two (22) car washes, nine 
(9) Jiffy Lube sites, and an InnovatelT equipment manufacturing company that provides operators with various 
technologies and advanced systems such as a reliable chemical dispensing system that consistently helps deliver clean 
cars in both conveyor and self service carwashes; a high-pressure wheel blaster, which is a touchless wheel cleaning 
system that automatically adjusts to conveyor speed; and a heavy-duty conveyor that is designed to maximize 
production. 
Transaction Overview / History 
In Jul-20, HCW secured $10MM in financing provided by Community Bank to expand the firm's footprint into central 
New York and to construct a new headquarters and warehouse in Colonie, NY. The recent financing is part of a string of 
investments that Hoffman has made to grow the Company's portfolio to approximately thirty (30) car washes within 
the next three (3) to five (5) years. InnovatelT Car Wash Equipment's growth mirrors that of the industry, and by late 
summer, HCW will be moving into a state-of-the-art 25,000-square-foot building, which it will share with the Hoffman 
business' office staff. Interest in the equipment has surged because it is durable and simple to maintain, and as an 
added benefit of manufacturing its own equipment, Hoffman Car Wash has able to utilize automation to minimize the 
impact of rising labor costs, which continue to escalate in New York. The new headquarters will house HCW's 20-
person office staff, which has outgrown the Company's existing corporate offices located at 1757 Central Avenue in 
Colonie, NY. The decision to expand HCW's footprint into central New York will also help to create more opportunities 
for the firm's employees. More locations will provide managers an opportunity to become district managers, while 
giving other staff opportunities to undertake new roles and responsibilities. The Company employs about 800 full— and 
part-time staff.

Ir Mammoth in  Holdings 
About Papa's Express Tunnel Car Wash 
Founded by Mark Philipp and his family in 2017, Papa's Express Tunnel Car Wash ("Papa's" or the "Company") 
is an express conveyor car wash located in Saratoga Springs, Utah. With an average volume of approximately 17,500 
cars washed daily, Papa's boasts a membership subscription base of roughly 4,200 unlimited monthly pass holders, 
equating to 70% of the Company's car washes. 
Transaction Overview / History 
In Oct-20, Mammoth Holdings, LLC ("Mammoth"), an Atlanta-based conveyor car wash operator, acquired Papa's 
Express Tunnel Car Wash ("Papa's"). Mammoth, which operates forty-siz (46) conveyor car washes, is the first car wash 
acquisition platform formed by industry-insiders and is the 8th largest express conveyor car wash operator in the 
United States. Mammoth is customer-focused operationally and operator-focused in its approach to acquisitions and 
seeks to be the partner-of-choice for car wash operators who desire liquidity, growth capital, and a tax-deferred equity 
investment opportunity. Mammoth's multi-brand portfolio includes Marc-1, Wash Me Fast, Swifty, Ultra, Finish 
Line, Wiggy Wash, Shine On, and PitStop, among others. Mammoth has significant growth capital at its disposal and is 
actively seeking acquisitions and development opportunities. In October 2018, Mammoth partnered with Red Dog 
Equity LLC, an Atlanta-based private equity firm, which, through its partnership with Tom Pritzker's family business 
interests (advised by The Pritzker Organization), provides the equity for Mammoth's corporate development initiatives.

About Mister Car Wash 
LEONARD GREEN 
& PARTNERS 
Founded in 1996, Mister Car Wash ("MCW" or the "Company") is the largest and fastest growing car wash chain in 
the United States with over 300+ locations, thirty-two (32) Oil Change Express centers, and more than 7,500 
employees. The Company's growth has been fueled by innovative technology, valued customers and investors and 
most importantly, motivated employees. The MCW brand is anchored in quality, speed, and customer care, allowing 
MCW to develop a reputation for providing high quality service at an affordable price. Innovative programs, such as the 
subscription-based Unlimited Wash Club, further increase customer value and enhance the customer experience. The 
Company focuses on the conveyor wash segment and washes over forty-five (45) million cars annually. 
Transaction Overview / History 
In 2007, UNCAP (the middle market private equity platform of Onex — one of the oldest and most successful private 
equity firms in North America with approximately $22B of assets under management, including $68 of Onex capital in 
private equity and credit securities) acquired majority interest in MCW. UNCAP helped to transform the Company from 
a small regional operator with geographic concentration in Houston into a market leader with over 180 locations 
operating in fourteen (14) states and generating more than $40MM of EBITDA. In August 2014, Leonard Green and 
Partners purchased the Company, generating a total of $458MM in realized proceeds to UNCAP, which represented a 
7.6x gross multiple of capital invested and a 34.6% gross IRR over the seven-year investment period according to 
representatives from ONCAP. 
In 2019, Penfund (an independent provider of junior capital to North American middle market companies), announced 
the completion of a follow-on investment in MCW as part of a small club of lenders providing a new $225MM second 
lien credit facility. The proceeds of this facility, together with the proceeds of a new $800MM first lien term loan, have 
been used to refinance MCW's existing debt and to pay a distribution to shareholders. Senior lenders also provided a 
new $75MM revolving credit facility and $40MM delayed draw term loan. 
Mister Car Wash (NYSE: MCW) made its public debut in June 2021, raising $468MM as shares quickly rallied to 49% 
above the IPO price of $15 per share. Mister Car Wash offered 37.5 million shares of common stock, with 31.25 million 
shares offered by the company and 6.25 million sold by existing shareholders. As of August 2021, the share price sits at 
$20.26 resulting in a total market cap of $6.12B. 
SPONSORSHIP / MANAGEMENT OVERVIEW (Cont.) 
l Russell Speeder's 
a Car Wash 
Mr. Shullman's successful career in the car wash industry began in 1984, when he served as co-owner of Detail Plus with his 
brother while attending Pace University (BA.). Upon graduation, Mr. Shullman took over management of Express Car Wash of 
Delray, where he was able to apply the management lessons he learned in college. Under his leadership, annual sales at the 
location grew from $425,000 to $840,000 within two (2) years through enhanced operating tactics and improved marketing 
strategies. In 1997, Mr. Shullman developed an automatic wheel-cleaning machine in use at all Express locations, which reduced 
processing time by 40% and labor costs by $25,000 per store per year. In recent years, Mr. Shullman has been responsible for 
Russell Speeder's Connecticut, Nebraska, Ohio, New York, Michigan and Missouri locations. A highly experienced operator and 
manager, Mr. Shullman has also expanded the firm's business to include management services, which the firm provides to other 
car wash owners seeking his operations skillset and prowess. Today, the Russell Speeder's business grosses over $48 million across 
twenty-three (23) locations. Over the course of his career, Mr. Shullman has invested significant time identifying and acquiring new 
locations, researching top-of-the-line operating techniques (as far away as Germany), and developing various marketing, operating, 
accounting, and human resource programs. From 2017-2020, Mr. Shullman implemented one of the most successful car wash 
subscription programs in the US. While most car washes either boast high subscription volumes at a low prices, or low subscription 
volumes at high prices, Mr. Shullman has achieved high subscription volumes at a high price through the implementation of the 
above-mentioned enhancements and programs. 
Additional Brand Overview 
*Shell 
Founded in 1907, Shell CHI Company is an international energy company with expertise in the exploration, production, refining and 
marketing of oil and natural gas, and the manufacturing of chemicals. Shell is the United States-based wholly owned subsidiary of 
Royal Dutch Shell, which is headquartered in The Hague, the Netherlands. Considered one of the largest oil companies in the world, 
Shell has over 80,000 employees and 25,000 Shell-branded gas stations throughout approximately 70 different countries. Shell is 
one of America's largest oil and natural gas producers. In 2020, Shell produced almost 4 million barrels of oil equivalent per day 
and accumulated $180 million in revenue. The company continues to progress towards cleaner energy solutions while delivering 
safe practices.

SPONSORSHIP / MANAGEMENT OVERVIEW 
THE MORGAN GROW 
The Morgan Group ("sponsor"), led IS principals Stuart Morgan, Scott Morgan, and Ryan Morgan, is a real estate 
investment and management company that owns and manages residential apartment buildings throughout the Greater New York 
City Area and in various markets throughout the country. Stuart Morgan has over thirty-eight (38) years of experience in the 
management and ownership of multifamily properties in the Bronx as well as various retail assets located throughout the country 
(including free-standing, single-tenant retail properties in PA, MS, OH, and KY). The Morgan Group's current portfolio consists of 
over 4,500 units across seventy-five (75) buildings, and consistently maintains an impressive average occupancy of over 99.0%. 
The Morgan Group is a highly capable property management firm that consistently invests monies back into its properties. This 
strategy, specifically in the Bronx, NY, enables the Sponsor to recoup investments in Major Capital Improvements ("MCI") and 
Apartment Improvements by allowing for rent increases in excess of those permitted by the New York City Rent Stabilization 
Guidelines Board. In addition, the Borrower can utilize J-51 Tax Abatements and Exemptions at 100% of "Approved" Improvement 
costs which reduces annual real estate tax payments during the Abatement/Exemption period. For a typical property, firm invests 
an average of $23,000 per unit in kitchen & bath modernizations, new plumbing risers and energy-related improvements. The 
Morgan Group implements these meticulous management practices and approaches across all properties in its portfolio. 
Rassr.I1 Speedy, s 
With roots dating back to 1964, Russell Speeder's Car Wash ("Sponsor"), led by President Michael Shullman, has 
emerged as a leading automotive servicing company specializing in car washes, detailing, hand waxing, and gasoline sales in the 
United States, with locations in Connecticut, Nebraska, Ohio, Florida, New York, Michigan, and Missouri (Sponsor Website: https:// 
www.russellspeeders.com/). In 2019, Russell Speeder's ranked #19 on Carwash.com's 'Top 50 U.S. Conveyor Chain' list, an annual 
account of the leading operators of conveyor/tunnel carwashes nationwide. 
Michael Shullman is a nationally recognized expert in the development, management, and operation of automotive businesses. 
Active in the industry for more than thirty-two (32) years, Mr. Shullman currently owns and operates twenty-three (23) facilities in 
six (6) states, and throughout his career has been involved over forty-six (46) projects under a variety of brands including Mobil, 
Phillips 66, Shell, Valvoline, and Russell Speeders. He has provided consulting and turnaround nationwide, more recently focusing 
on opportunistic acquisitions of underperforming automotive businesses, and is active in trade associations on local, state, and 
national levels. Mr. Shullman also holds an award winning patent.

Russell Speeder's 
MARKET / SUBMARKET INFORMATION 
Old Greenwich, Connecticut 
A coastal neighborhood situated within Fairfield County, Old Greenwich is in the southeast corner of the town of Greenwich. It is 
bounded by the Long Island Sound and the neighboring city of Stamford. Established in 1640, the town has held onto its historical 
roots, allowing it to be deemed the oldest neighborhood in Greenwich. Consequently, Old Greenwich has a substantial amount of 
history throughout the town. Today, the region is primarily a suburban residential area with a solid commercial base and a good 
industrial sector. In general, the communities in southwestern Fairfield County and along the coast of the Long Island Sound are 
more prestigious, middle-to upper-Income areas. Based on Bloomberg's annual report regarding "America's 100 Richest Places," 
Old Greenwich ranks seventh (7th) among the wealthiest communities in the country. Although Old Greenwich has a population of 
around 6,100 according to the 2010 census, it maintains a small-town feel for locals and visitors alike. There are plenty of offerings 
from shopping to dining. The downtown shopping district features a block-long strip of mom-and-pop boutiques along with 
popular and diverse restaurants. There are numerous attractions such as clean beaches to major public green spaces. Considered a 
family-oriented town, Old Greenwich has a highly rated public and private school system. The elementary school through high 
school boasts A-A+ ratings on niche.com, making the area a prime attraction for families. 
The County of Fairfield is home to four of Connecticut's most dynamic metropolitan areas (Stamford, Norwalk, Bridgeport and 
Danbury). Its strategic location in the Southwestern sector of Connecticut offers easy access to the New York Metropolitan area 
and all of New England. As a result, the region has a diverse workforce with nineteen (19) Fortune 1000 corporations stationed 
within Fairfield County. There are multiple public and private colleges and universities settled in the County, such as Fairfield 
University, Sacred Heart University, and University of Bridgeport. The primary means of transportation throughout the region is by 
automobile. Interstate 95, which extends along the entire eastern seaboard from Maine to Florida, is the major area highway. The 
Merritt Parkway, which runs parallel to 1-95, traverses the county east and west provides a significant commuter route. In addition, 
Route 1. also provides local access from the surrounding communities.

Russell Speeder's 
EXECUTIVE SUMMARY 
An investor group consisting of The Morgan Group and Russell Speeder's Car Wash (collectively known as the "Sponsor" or 
"Borrower") is seeking first mortgage financing in the amount of $13,000,000 ($650 PSF / 65% LTC) to finance the acquisition of a 
conveyorized-tunnel car wash and Shell gasoline station located at 1429 East Putnam Avenue, Old Greenwich, CT 06870 ("The 
Property"). With a purchase price of $20,000,000 ($1,000 PSF), the Property spans roughly 20,000 SF and is fully-outfitted with 
complete car wash systems, equipment, car wash tunnels, equipment rooms, enhanced computer systems, and self-serve 
vacuums. The asset boasts multiple revenue streams due to its attached oil change and emissions testing center, convenience 
store, and Shell gasoline station. As of August 2021, the Property has 5,600 members each paying $40 per month for the use of its 
conveyorized-car wash. Generating an additional $2,688,000 per year, the asset will conclude 2021 with an EBITDA of over 
$4,000,000. Given Its prime location and addition of the Russell Speeder's brand, the Property is poised to grow Its already-high 
customer volumes and further increase its subscription-base. Russell Speeder's subscription-based business model has resulted in 
unparalleled customer retention and loyalty, with an overwhelming majority of customers renewing this unique 'Netflix-type' 
subscription service on a monthly basis. More specifically, subscription wash revenue accounts for approximately 85% of total wash 
revenue across their entire portfolio. A direct result of the firm's exceptional management team and operation practices, coupled 
with the brand's top-of-the-line customer service and quality care, the Sponsor has successfully grown cash flows throughout its 
portfolio in a significant manner since 2016. In 2019, Russell Speeder's ranked #19 on Carwash.com's 'Top 50 U.S. Conveyor Chain' 
list, an annual account of the leading operators of conveyor/tunnel carwashes nationwide. The Property is located in proximity to 
several major arteries and thoroughfares within the greater Fairfield County, resulting in high visibility, vehicle traffic counts, and 
positive sales volumes. The loan proceeds will be used to acquire the property and cover associated closing costs. 
The Sponsorship group boasts decades of industry experience and proven track records: The Morgan Group, led by principals 
Stuart Morgan (over thirty-eight (38) years of industry experience), Scott Morgan, and Ryan Morgan, is a real estate Investment 
and management company that owns and manages residential apartment buildings throughout the Greater New York City Area 
and retail properties in various markets throughout the country; Russell Speeder's Car Wash is a nationally recognized expert in the 
development, management, and operation of automotive businesses. Active in the industry for more than thirty-two (32) years, 
Michael Shullman currently owns and operates twenty-three (23) facilities in six (6) states and has been involved over forty-six (46) 
projects throughout his career under a variety of brands including Mobil, Phillips 66, Shell, Valvoline, and Russell Speeders.

Overview of Valuations 
Ca rwashes' meteoric rise in popularity has created much 
confusion, uncertainty, and change in valuations over the 
past five years. For decades prior to the recent boom, 
performing carwashes traded at relatively stable and 
predictable, albeit largely more opaque from an external 
investors lens, levels. Historically, carwashes have traded for 
4- 6x EWEBITDA multiples (inclusive of real estate). 
Throughout the past half a decade, several factors have 
come into play that have caused radical shifts and changes 
in valuations. Main events and influencers include the going 
public of Mister Car Wash and Driven Brands, the general 
boon of institutional investor group and fund involvement in 
the space, and the proliferation of sale-leasebacks 
throughout the industry. 
For an industry that has largely been ignored by the general 
investing public, the level of increased interest and newly 
founded external party demanded desire for clarity in 
"appropriate" multiples and valuations, has created an 
abundance of misinformation and a lacking general 
consensus as to answers concerning valuations.

The Canvas: Saturation vs. Whitespace 
Regardless of how measured, significant whitespace still present throughout the United States 
Summary & Thoughts 
One of the most frequently asked and debated questions in the car wash industry is whether 
the U.S. market is saturated or if there is still ample whitespace to grow. This question lies at the 
very core of many critical decisions. For individual operators, their perspective on this issue 
often determines whether to double down on existing operations or embark on a new build. 
For institutional investors, this view fundamentally shapes the investment thesis. 
The short answer is that the country as a whole is not saturated with express exterior car 
washes. While there are undoubtedly specific regions—and even localities—where saturation is 
severe, it would be misleading to generalize this across the entire nation. Viewing the market 
through a broad-stroke or thematic lens can be particularly hazardous, especially for investors 
executing densification-based strategies. Saying a part of the country, a state, or even a town is 
or isn't saturated often lacks meaning without proper context or nuance. 
There are several methodologies for assessing the current level of market saturation, each with 
its own limitations and deficiencies. However, regardless of the approach taken, the data 
suggests that there is still +50% growth potential for incremental express exterior car washes in 
the U.S. The more challenging —and ultimately more impactful—question is determining which 
types of parties and groups are best suited to capture and capitalize on this remaining 
whitespace. These "knights" of the industry will define the next phase of growth.

Executive Summary 
Despite all that's changed, the reasons to be in the carwash industry have not 
The car wash industry has experienced a truly transformative past five years. A 
massive influx of investor interest and institutional capital has fueled exponential 
growth, driving the rapid adoption of operational and technological 
advancements, alongside unprecedented levels of new builds and 
developments. In many ways, the industry today is nearly unrecognizable 
compared to just five years ago. 
Investor activity, particularly from financial sponsors, appeared relentless. The 
broader market seemed bewitched by the allure of the industry. From an 
outsider's perspective, it was as though they had unearthed the very definition of 
a diamond in the rough—hidden just beneath a thin layer of dirt, overlooked by 
many yet tantalizingly within reach. With this shared mentality, private equity 
investors converged en masse, pouring capital into the sector in a frenzy. The 
industry's potential appeared boundless, offering gains and opportunities that 
captured the imagination of both investors and operators alike. This surge of 
interest and activity became almost axiomatic, as the car wash industry seemingly 
embodied everything institutional investors seek: scalability, profitability, and 
untapped potential. 
Spurred on by institutional investment, the industry underwent a near-
renaissance in operational practices, equipment, and technology. These past five 
years saw the most significant and widespread adoption of unlimited wash 
membership programs to date. Innovations such as license plate recognition 
systems and the strategic use of social media marketing further elevated 
operational standards. The pace and scale of these advancements were 
unmatched, in many ways redefining what was possible within the industry. 
Beyond M&A activity and technological improvements, the period also saw an 
unprecedented surge in new car wash developments across the country. These 
new builds, coupled with the sector's evolving operational and technological 
landscape, reshaped the industry at an astonishing pace. 
The past five years have ushered in monumental changes—each significant in its 
own right and collectively transformative. It would be easy to believe the industry 
has become something entirely new, but that is not the case. 
When I founded Car Wash Advisory in August 2019, it wasn't due to any 
clairvoyance or premonition. My decision was born from a deep admiration for 
the industry and its people. From my first exposure, I was captivated by the 
strength, resilience, and genuine nature of those who make up this sector. To this 
day, the car wash industry remains home to some of the most value-driven and 
remarkable individuals I have ever met. Despite the dramatic surface-level 
changes of the past five years, this defining characteristic of the industry remains 
as true as ever. 
This industry, along with its irreplaceable operators and supporters, has given 
me opportunities and experiences over the past five years that I wouldn't trade 
for the world. For this, I am deeply grateful and forever indebted. Through 
publishing content like this report, I hope to repay this debt in the best way I 
can—by paying it forward and contributing to the ongoing growth and 
understanding of this incredible industry. 
Sincerely,
